1855      /**
1856       * Instantiates the serializer group sub-builder.
1857       *
1858       * @return A new serializer group sub-builder.
1859       */
1860      protected SerializerSet.Builder createSerializers() {
1861         return SerializerSet.create().beanContext(beanContext());
1862      }
1863
1864      /**
1865       * Serializer.
1866       *
1867       * <p>
1868       * Associates the specified {@link Serializer Serializer} with the HTTP client.
1869       *
1870       * <p>
1871       * The serializer is used to serialize POJOs into the HTTP request body.
1872       *
1873       * <ul class='notes'>
1874       *    <li class='note'>When using this method that takes in a class, the serializer can be configured using any of the serializer property setters (e.g. {@link #sortCollections()}) or
1875       *    bean context property setters (e.g. {@link #swaps(Class...)}) defined on this builder class.
1876       * </ul>
1877       *
1878       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
1879       * <p class='bjava'>
1880       *    <jc>// Create a client that uses JSON transport for request bodies.</jc>
1881       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
1882       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
1883       *       .serializer(JsonSerializer.<jk>class</jk>)
1884       *       .sortCollections()  <jc>// Sort any collections being serialized.</jc>
1885       *       .build();
1886       * </p>
1887       *
1888       * @param value
1889       *    The new value for this setting.
1890       *    <br>The default is {@link JsonSerializer}.
1891       * @return This object.
1892       */
1893      @SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
1894      @FluentSetter
1895      public Builder serializer(Class<? extends Serializer> value) {
1896         return serializers(value);
1897      }
1898
1899      /**
1900       * Serializer.
1901       *
1902       * <p>
1903       * Associates the specified {@link Serializer Serializer} with the HTTP client.
1904       *
1905       * <p>
1906       * The serializer is used to serialize POJOs into the HTTP request body.
1907       *
1908       * <ul class='notes'>
1909       *    <li class='note'>When using this method that takes in a pre-instantiated serializer, the serializer property setters (e.g. {@link #sortCollections()}) or
1910       *    bean context property setters (e.g. {@link #swaps(Class...)}) defined
1911       *    on this builder class have no effect.
1912       * </ul>
1913       *
1914       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
1915       * <p class='bjava'>
1916       *    <jc>// Create a client that uses a predefined JSON serializer request bodies.</jc>
1917       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
1918       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
1919       *       .serializer(JsonSerializer.<jsf>DEFAULT_READABLE</jsf>)
1920       *       .build();
1921       * </p>
1922       *
1923       * @param value
1924       *    The new value for this setting.
1925       *    <br>The default is {@link JsonSerializer}.
1926       * @return This object.
1927       */
1928      @FluentSetter
1929      public Builder serializer(Serializer value) {
1930         return serializers(value);
1931      }
1932
1933      /**
1934       * Serializers.
1935       *
1936       * <p>
1937       * Associates the specified {@link Serializer Serializers} with the HTTP client.
1938       *
1939       * <p>
1940       * The serializer is used to serialize POJOs into the HTTP request body.
1941       *
1942       * <p>
1943       * The serializer that best matches the <c>Content-Type</c> header will be used to serialize the request body.
1944       * <br>If no <c>Content-Type</c> header is specified, the first serializer in the list will be used.
1945       *
1946       * <ul class='notes'>
1947       *    <li class='note'>When using this method that takes in classes, the serializers can be configured using any of the serializer property setters (e.g. {@link #sortCollections()}) or
1948       *    bean context property setters (e.g. {@link #swaps(Class...)}) defined on this builder class.
1949       * </ul>
1950       *
1951       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
1952       * <p class='bjava'>
1953       *    <jc>// Create a client that uses JSON and XML transport for request bodies.</jc>
1954       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
1955       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
1956       *       .serializers(JsonSerializer.<jk>class</jk>, XmlSerializer.<jk>class</jk>)
1957       *       .sortCollections()  <jc>// Sort any collections being serialized.</jc>
1958       *       .build();
1959       * </p>
1960       *
1961       * @param value
1962       *    The new value for this setting.
1963       *    <br>The default is {@link JsonSerializer}.
1964       * @return This object.
1965       */
1966      @SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
1967      @FluentSetter
1968      public Builder serializers(Class<? extends Serializer>...value) {
1969         serializers().add(value);
1970         return this;
1971      }
1972
1973      /**
1974       * Serializers.
1975       *
1976       * <p>
1977       * Associates the specified {@link Serializer Serializers} with the HTTP client.
1978       *
1979       * <p>
1980       * The serializer is used to serialize POJOs into the HTTP request body.
1981       *
1982       * <p>
1983       * The serializer that best matches the <c>Content-Type</c> header will be used to serialize the request body.
1984       * <br>If no <c>Content-Type</c> header is specified, the first serializer in the list will be used.
1985       *
1986       * <ul class='notes'>
1987       *    <li class='note'>When using this method that takes in a pre-instantiated serializers, the serializer property setters (e.g. {@link #sortCollections()}) or
1988       *    bean context property setters (e.g. {@link #swaps(Class...)}) defined
1989       *    on this builder class have no effect.
1990       * </ul>
1991       *
1992       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
1993       * <p class='bjava'>
1994       *    <jc>// Create a client that uses predefined JSON and XML serializers for request bodies.</jc>
1995       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
1996       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
1997       *       .serializers(JsonSerializer.<jsf>DEFAULT_READABLE</jsf>, XmlSerializer.<jsf>DEFAULT_READABLE</jsf>)
1998       *       .build();
1999       * </p>
2000       *
2001       * @param value
2002       *    The new value for this setting.
2003       *    <br>The default is {@link JsonSerializer}.
2004       * @return This object.
2005       */
2006      @FluentSetter
2007      public Builder serializers(Serializer...value) {
2008         serializers().add(value);
2009         return this;
2010      }

2432      /**
2433       * Returns the builder for the list of headers that get applied to all requests created by this builder.
2434       *
2435       * <p>
2436       * This is the primary method for accessing the request header list.
2437       * On first call, the builder is created via the method {@link #createHeaderData()}.
2438       *
2439       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
2440       * <p class='bjava'>
2441       *    <jc>// Create a client that adds a "Foo: bar" header on every request.</jc>
2442       *    RestClient.Builder <jv>builder</jv> = RestClient.<jsm>create</jsm>();
2443       *    <jv>builder</jv>.headerData().setDefault(<js>"Foo"</js>, <js>"bar"</js>));
2444       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = <jv>builder</jv>.build();
2445       * </p>
2446       *
2447       * <p>
2448       * The following convenience methods are also provided for updating the headers:
2449       * <ul>
2450       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #headers(Header...)}
2451       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #headersDefault(Header...)}
2452       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #header(String,String)}
2453       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #header(String,Supplier)}
2454       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #mediaType(String)}
2455       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #mediaType(MediaType)}
2456       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #accept(String)}
2457       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #acceptCharset(String)}
2458       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #clientVersion(String)}
2459       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #contentType(String)}
2460       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #debug()}
2461       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #noTrace()}
2462       * </ul>
2463       *
2464       * <p>
2465       * Note that the {@link #headers(Consumer)} method can be used to call this method without breaking fluent call chains.
2466       *
2467       * @return The header list builder.
2468       */
2469      public final HeaderList.Builder headers() {
2470         if (headerData == null)
2471            headerData = createHeaderData();
2472         return headerData;
2473      }
2474
2475      /**
2476       * Applies an operation to the header data builder.
2477       *
2478       * <p>
2479       * Typically used to allow you to execute operations without breaking the fluent flow of the client builder.
2480       *
2481       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
2482       * <p class='bjava'>
2483       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
2484       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
2485       *       .headerData(<jv>x</jv> -&gt; <jv>x</jv>.setDefault(<js>"Foo"</js>, <js>"bar"</js>))
2486       *       .build();
2487       * </p>
2488       *
2489       * @param operation The operation to apply.
2490       * @return This object.
2491       */
2492      public final Builder headers(Consumer<HeaderList.Builder> operation) {
2493         operation.accept(headers());
2494         return this;
2495      }
2496
2497      /**
2498       * Creates the builder for the header list.
2499       *
2500       * <p>
2501       * Subclasses can override this method to provide their own implementation.
2502       *
2503       * <p>
2504       * The default behavior creates an empty builder.
2505       *
2506       * @return The header list builder.
2507       * @see #headers()
2508       */
2509      protected HeaderList.Builder createHeaderData() {
2510         return HeaderList.create();
2511      }
2512
2513      /**
2514       * Appends multiple headers to all requests.
2515       *
2516       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
2517       * <p class='bjava'>
2518       *    <jk>import static</jk> org.apache.juneau.http.HttpHeaders.*;
2519       *
2520       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
2521       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
2522       *       .headers(
2523       *          <jsf>ACCEPT_TEXT_XML</jsf>,
2524       *          <jsm>stringHeader</jsm>(<js>"Foo"</js>, <js>"bar"</js>)
2525       *       )
2526       *       .build();
2527       * </p>
2528       *
2529       * <p>
2530       * This is a shortcut for calling <c>headerData().append(<jv>parts</jv>)</c>.
2531       *
2532       * @param parts
2533       *    The header to set.
2534       * @return This object.
2535       * @see #headers()
2536       */
2537      @FluentSetter
2538      public Builder headers(Header...parts) {
2539         headers().append(parts);
2540         return this;
2541      }
2542
2543      /**
2544       * Sets default header values.
2545       *
2546       * <p>
2547       * Uses default values for specified headers if not otherwise specified on the outgoing requests.
2548       *
2549       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
2550       * <p class='bjava'>
2551       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
2552       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
2553       *       .headersDefault(<jsm>stringHeader</jsm>(<js>"Foo"</js>, ()-&gt;<js>"bar"</js>));
2554       *       .build();
2555       * </p>
2556       *
2557       * <p>
2558       * This is a shortcut for calling <c>headerData().setDefault(<jv>parts</jv>)</c>.
2559       *
2560       * @param parts The header values.
2561       * @return This object.
2562       * @see #headers()
2563       */
2564      public Builder headersDefault(Header...parts) {
2565         headers().setDefault(parts);
2566         return this;
2567      }
2568
2569      /**
2570       * Appends a header to all requests.
2571       *
2572       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
2573       * <p class='bjava'>
2574       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
2575       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
2576       *       .header(<js>"Foo"</js>, <js>"bar"</js>);
2577       *       .build();
2578       * </p>
2579       *
2580       * <p>
2581       * This is a shortcut for calling <c>headerData().append(<jv>name</jv>,<jv>value</jv>)</c>.
2582       *
2583       * @param name The header name.
2584       * @param value The header value.
2585       * @return This object.
2586       * @see #headers()
2587       */
2588      @FluentSetter

2591         return this;

2635         return headers(Accept.of(value), ContentType.of(value));

2722      /**

2724       *
2725       * <p>
2726       * This is a shortcut for calling <c>headerData().append(Debug.<jsm>of</jsm>(<jv>value</jv>))</c>.
2727       *
2728       * @return This object.
2729       * @see #headers()
2730       */
2731      @Override
2732      @FluentSetter
2733      public Builder debug() {
2734         super.debug();
2735         serializers().forEach(x -> x.debug());
2736         return headers(Debug.TRUE);

2739      /**
2740       * When called, <c>No-Trace: true</c> is added to requests.
2741       *
2742       * <p>
2743       * This gives the opportunity for the servlet to not log errors on invalid requests.
2744       * This is useful for testing purposes when you don't want your log file to show lots of errors that are simply the
2745       * results of testing.
2746       *
2747       * <p>
2748       * It's up to the server to decide whether to allow for this.
2749       * The <c>BasicTestRestLogger</c> class watches for this header and prevents logging of status 400+ responses to
2750       * prevent needless logging of test scenarios.
2751       *
2752       * @return This object.
2753       * @see #headers()
2754       */
2755      @FluentSetter
2756      public Builder noTrace() {
2757         return headers(NoTrace.of(true));
2758      }

2763
2764      /**
2765       * Returns the builder for the list of query parameters that get applied to all requests created by this builder.
2766       *
2767       * <p>
2768       * This is the primary method for accessing the query parameter list.
2769       * On first call, the builder is created via the method {@link #createQueryData()}.
2770       *
2771       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
2772       * <p class='bjava'>
2773       *    <jc>// Create a client that adds a "foo=bar" query parameter on every request.</jc>
2774       *    RestClient.Builder <jv>builder</jv> = RestClient.<jsm>create</jsm>();
2775       *    <jv>builder</jv>.queryData().setDefault(<js>"foo"</js>, <js>"bar"</js>));
2776       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = <jv>builder</jv>.build();
2777       * </p>
2778       *
2779       * <p>
2780       * The following convenience methods are also provided for updating the parameters:
2781       * <ul>
2782       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #queryData(NameValuePair...)}
2783       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #queryDataDefault(NameValuePair...)}
2784       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #queryData(String,String)}
2785       *    <li class='jm'>{@link #queryData(String,Supplier)}
2786       * </ul>
2787       *
2788       * <p>
2789       * Note that the {@link #queryData(Consumer)} method can be used to call this method without breaking fluent call chains.
2790       *
2791       * @return The query data list builder.
2792       */
2793      public final PartList.Builder queryData() {
2794         if (queryData == null)
2795            queryData = createQueryData();
2796         return queryData;
2797      }
2798
2799      /**
2800       * Applies an operation to the query data builder.
2801       *
2802       * <p>
2803       * Typically used to allow you to execute operations without breaking the fluent flow of the client builder.
2804       *
2805       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
2806       * <p class='bjava'>
2807       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
2808       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
2809       *       .queryData(<jv>x</jv> -&gt; <jv>x</jv>.setDefault(<js>"foo"</js>, <js>"bar"</js>))
2810       *       .build();
2811       * </p>
2812       *
2813       * @param operation The operation to apply.
2814       * @return This object.
2815       */
2816      public final Builder queryData(Consumer<PartList.Builder> operation) {
2817         operation.accept(queryData());
2818         return this;
2819      }
2820

2822       * Creates the builder for the query data list.
2823       *
2824       * <p>
2825       * Subclasses can override this method to provide their own implementation.
2826       *
2827       * <p>
2828       * The default behavior creates an empty builder.
2829       *
2830       * @return The query data list builder.
2831       * @see #queryData()
2832       */
2833      protected PartList.Builder createQueryData() {
2834         return PartList.create();
2835      }

3212       *       .pathData(
3213       *          <jsm>stringPart</jsm>(<js>"foo"</js>, <js>"bar"</js>),
3214       *          <jsm>booleanPart</jsm>(<js>"baz"</js>, <jk>true</jk>)
3215       *       )
3216       *       .build();
3217       * </p>
3218       *
3219       * <p>
3220       * This is a shortcut for calling <c>pathData().append(<jv>parts</jv>)</c>.
3221       *
3222       * @param parts
3223       *    The path parameters.
3224       * @return This object.
3225       * @see #pathData()
3226       */
3227      @FluentSetter
3228      public Builder pathData(NameValuePair...parts) {
3229         pathData().append(parts);
3230         return this;
3231      }

3310      // callHandler

3312
3313      /**
3314       * Returns the creator for the rest call handler.
3315       *
3316       * <p>
3317       * Allows you to provide a custom handler for making HTTP calls.
3318       *
3319       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3320       * <p class='bjava'>
3321       *    <jc>// Create a client that handles processing of requests using a custom handler.</jc>
3322       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyRestCallHandler <jk>implements</jk> RestCallHandler {
3323       *
3324       *       <ja>@Override</ja>
3325       *       <jk>public</jk> HttpResponse run(HttpHost <jv>target</jv>, HttpRequest <jv>request</jv>, HttpContext <jv>context</jv>) <jk>throws</jk> IOException {
3326       *          <jc>// Custom handle requests.</jc>
3327       *       }
3328       *    }
3329       *
3330       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3331       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3332       *       .callHandler(MyRestCallHandler.<jk>class</jk>)
3333       *       .build();
3334       * </p>
3335       *
3336       * <ul class='notes'>
3337       *    <li class='note'>
3338       *       The {@link RestClient#run(HttpHost, HttpRequest, HttpContext)} method can also be overridden to produce the same results.
3339       *    <li class='note'>
3340       *       Use {@link BeanCreator#impl(Object)} to specify an already instantiated instance.
3341       *    <li class='note'>
3342       *       Use {@link BeanCreator#type(Class)} to specify a subtype to instantiate.
3343       *       <br>Subclass must have a public constructor that takes in any args available
3344       *       in the bean store of this builder (including {@link RestClient} itself).
3345       * </ul>
3346       *
3347       * <ul class='seealso'>
3348       *    <li class='jic'>{@link RestCallHandler}
3349       * </ul>
3350       *
3351       * @return The creator for the rest call handler.
3352       */
3353      public final BeanCreator<RestCallHandler> callHandler() {
3354         if (callHandler == null)
3355            callHandler = createCallHandler();
3356         return callHandler;
3357      }
3358
3359      /**
3360       * Applies an operation to the REST call handler bean creator.
3361       *
3362       * <p>
3363       * Typically used to allow you to execute operations without breaking the fluent flow of the client builder.
3364       *
3365       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3366       * <p class='bjava'>
3367       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3368       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3369       *       .callHandler(<jv>x</jv> -&gt; <jv>x</jv>.impl(<jv>myCallHandler</jv>))
3370       *       .build();
3371       * </p>
3372       *
3373       * @param operation The operation to apply.
3374       * @return This object.
3375       */
3376      public final Builder callHandler(Consumer<BeanCreator<RestCallHandler>> operation) {
3377         operation.accept(callHandler());
3378         return this;
3379      }
3380
3381      /**
3382       * Creates the creator for the rest call handler.
3383       *
3384       * <p>
3385       * Subclasses can override this method to provide their own implementation.
3386       *
3387       * <p>
3388       * The default behavior creates a bean creator initialized to return a {@link BasicRestCallHandler}.
3389       *
3390       * @return The creator for the rest call handler.
3391       * @see #callHandler()
3392       */
3393      protected BeanCreator<RestCallHandler> createCallHandler() {
3394         return beanStore.createBean(RestCallHandler.class).type(BasicRestCallHandler.class);
3395      }

3398       * REST call handler class.
3399       *
3400       * <p>
3401       * Specifies a custom handler for making HTTP calls.
3402       *
3403       * <p>
3404       * This is a shortcut for <c>callHandler().type(<jv>value</jv>)</c>.
3405       *
3406       * @param value
3407       *    The new value for this setting.
3408       * @return This object.
3409       * @see #callHandler()
3410       */
3411      @FluentSetter
3412      public Builder callHandler(Class<? extends RestCallHandler> value) {
3413         callHandler().type(value);
3414         return this;
3415      }

3465       *    <jc>// Construct a client that logs messages to a special logger.</jc>
3466       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3467       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3468       *       .logger(Logger.<jsm>getLogger</jsm>(<js>"MyLogger"</js>))  <jc>// Log to MyLogger logger.</jc>
3469       *       .logToConsole()  <jc>// Also log to console.</jc>
3470       *       .logRequests(<jsf>FULL</jsf>, <jsf>WARNING</jsf>)  <jc>// Log requests with full detail at WARNING level.</jc>
3471       *       .build();
3472       * </p>
3473       *
3474       * @param value The logger to use for logging.
3475       * @return This object.
3476       */
3477      @FluentSetter

3492       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3493       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3494       *       .logToConsole()
3495       *       .logRequests(<jsf>FULL</jsf>, <jsf>INFO</jsf>)  <jc>// Level is ignored when logging to console.</jc>
3496       *       .build();
3497       * </p>

3500       */

3502      public Builder logToConsole() {

3507      /**
3508       * Log requests.
3509       *
3510       * <p>
3511       * Causes requests/responses to be logged at the specified log level at the end of the request.
3512       *
3513       * <p>
3514       * <jsf>SIMPLE</jsf> detail produces a log message like the following:
3515       * <p class='bconsole'>
3516       *    POST http://localhost:10000/testUrl, HTTP/1.1 200 OK
3517       * </p>
3518       *
3519       * <p>
3520       * <jsf>FULL</jsf> detail produces a log message like the following:
3521       * <p class='bconsole'>
3522       *    === HTTP Call (outgoing) =======================================================
3523       *    === REQUEST ===
3524       *    POST http://localhost:10000/testUrl
3525       *    ---request headers---
3526       *       Debug: true
3527       *       No-Trace: true
3528       *       Accept: application/json
3529       *    ---request entity---
3530       *       Content-Type: application/json
3531       *    ---request content---
3532       *    {"foo":"bar","baz":123}
3533       *    === RESPONSE ===
3534       *    HTTP/1.1 200 OK
3535       *    ---response headers---
3536       *       Content-Type: application/json;charset=utf-8
3537       *       Content-Length: 21
3538       *       Server: Jetty(8.1.0.v20120127)
3539       *    ---response content---
3540       *    {"message":"OK then"}
3541       *    === END ========================================================================
3542       * </p>
3543       *
3544       * <p>
3545       * By default, the message is logged to the default logger.  It can be logged to a different logger via the
3546       * {@link #logger(Logger)} method or logged to the console using the
3547       * {@link #logToConsole()} method.
3548       *
3549       * @param detail The detail level of logging.
3550       * @param level The log level.
3551       * @param test A predicate to use per-request to see if the request should be logged.  If <jk>null</jk>, always logs.
3552       * @return This object.
3553       */
3554      @FluentSetter
3555      public Builder logRequests(DetailLevel detail, Level level, BiPredicate<RestRequest,RestResponse> test) {
3556         logRequests = detail;
3557         logRequestsLevel = level;
3558         logRequestsPredicate = test;
3559         return this;
3560      }

3563      // HttpClientConnectionManager methods.

3565
3566      /**
3567       * Creates the {@link HttpClientConnectionManager} returned by {@link #createConnectionManager()}.
3568       *
3569       * <p>
3570       * Subclasses can override this method to provide their own connection manager.
3571       *
3572       * <p>
3573       * The default implementation returns an instance of a {@link PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager} if {@link #pooled()}
3574       * was called or {@link BasicHttpClientConnectionManager} if not..
3575       *
3576       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3577       * <p class='bjava'>
3578       *    <jc>// A Builder that provides it's own customized HttpClientConnectionManager.</jc>
3579       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyBuilder <jk>extends</jk> Builder {
3580       *       <ja>@Override</ja>
3581       *       <jk>protected</jk> HttpClientConnectionManager createConnectionManager() {
3582       *          <jk>return new</jk> PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager();
3583       *       }
3584       *    }
3585       *
3586       *    <jc>// Instantiate.</jc>
3587       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = <jk>new</jk> MyBuilder().build();
3588       * </p>
3589       *
3590       * @return The HTTP client builder to use to create the HTTP client.
3591       */
3592      protected HttpClientConnectionManager createConnectionManager() {
3593         return (pooled ? new PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager() : new BasicHttpClientConnectionManager());
3594      }
3595
3596      /**
3597       * When called, the {@link #createConnectionManager()} method will return a {@link PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager}
3598       * instead of a {@link BasicHttpClientConnectionManager}.
3599       *
3600       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3601       * <p class='bjava'>
3602       *    <jc>// Construct a client that uses pooled connections.</jc>
3603       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3604       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3605       *       .pooled()
3606       *       .build();
3607       * </p>
3608       *
3609       * @return This object.
3610       */
3611      @FluentSetter
3612      public Builder pooled() {
3613         this.pooled = true;
3614         return this;
3615      }
3616
3617      /**
3618       * Assigns {@link HttpClientConnectionManager} instance.
3619       *
3620       * @param value New property value.
3621       * @return This object.
3622       * @see HttpClientBuilder#setConnectionManager(HttpClientConnectionManager)
3623       */
3624      @FluentSetter
3625      public Builder connectionManager(HttpClientConnectionManager value) {
3626         connectionManager = value;
3627         httpClientBuilder().setConnectionManager(value);
3628         return this;
3629      }

3631      /**
3632       * Defines the connection manager is to be shared by multiple client instances.
3633       *
3634       * <ul class='notes'>
3635       *    <li class='note'>If the connection manager is shared its life-cycle is expected to be managed by the caller and it will not be shut down if the client is closed.
3636       * </ul>
3637       *
3638       * @param shared New property value.
3639       * @return This object.
3640       * @see HttpClientBuilder#setConnectionManagerShared(boolean)
3641       */
3642      @FluentSetter
3643      public Builder connectionManagerShared(boolean shared) {
3644         httpClientBuilder().setConnectionManagerShared(shared);
3645         return this;
3646      }
3647
3648      /**
3649       * Set up this client to use BASIC auth.
3650       *
3651       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3652       * <p class='bjava'>
3653       *    <jc>// Construct a client that uses BASIC authentication.</jc>
3654       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3655       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3656       *       .basicAuth(<js>"http://localhost"</js>, 80, <js>"me"</js>, <js>"mypassword"</js>)
3657       *       .build();
3658       * </p>
3659       *
3660       * @param host The auth scope hostname.
3661       * @param port The auth scope port.
3662       * @param user The username.
3663       * @param pw The password.
3664       * @return This object.
3665       */
3666      @FluentSetter
3667      public Builder basicAuth(String host, int port, String user, String pw) {
3668         AuthScope scope = new AuthScope(host, port);
3669         Credentials up = new UsernamePasswordCredentials(user, pw);
3670         CredentialsProvider p = new BasicCredentialsProvider();
3671         p.setCredentials(scope, up);
3672         defaultCredentialsProvider(p);
3673         return this;
3674      }

3687       *    The new value for this setting.

3690      @FluentSetter

3695
3696      /**
3697       * <i><l>RestClient</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Executor service.
3698       *
3699       * <p>
3700       * Defines the executor service to use when calling future methods on the {@link RestRequest} class.
3701       *
3702       * <p>
3703       * This executor service is used to create {@link Future} objects on the following methods:
3704       * <ul>
3705       *    <li class='jm'>{@link RestRequest#runFuture()}
3706       *    <li class='jm'>{@link RestRequest#completeFuture()}
3707       *    <li class='jm'>{@link ResponseContent#asFuture(Class)} (and similar methods)
3708       * </ul>
3709       *
3710       * <p>
3711       * The default executor service is a single-threaded {@link ThreadPoolExecutor} with a 30 second timeout
3712       * and a queue size of 10.
3713       *
3714       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3715       * <p class='bjava'>
3716       *    <jc>// Create a client with a customized executor service.</jc>
3717       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3718       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3719       *       .executorService(<jk>new</jk> ThreadPoolExecutor(1, 1, 30, TimeUnit.<jsf>SECONDS</jsf>, <jk>new</jk> ArrayBlockingQueue&lt;Runnable&gt;(10)), <jk>true</jk>)
3720       *       .build();
3721       *
3722       *    <jc>// Use it to asynchronously run a request.</jc>
3723       *    Future&lt;RestResponse&gt; <jv>responseFuture</jv> = <jv>client</jv>.get(<jsf>URI</jsf>).runFuture();
3724       *
3725       *    <jc>// Do some other stuff.</jc>
3726       *
3727       *    <jc>// Now read the response.</jc>
3728       *    String <jv>body</jv> = <jv>responseFuture</jv>.get().getContent().asString();
3729       *
3730       *    <jc>// Use it to asynchronously retrieve a response.</jc>
3731       *    Future&lt;MyBean&gt; <jv>myBeanFuture</jv> = <jv>client</jv>
3732       *       .get(<jsf>URI</jsf>)
3733       *       .run()
3734       *       .getContent().asFuture(MyBean.<jk>class</jk>);
3735       *
3736       *    <jc>// Do some other stuff.</jc>
3737       *
3738       *    <jc>// Now read the response.</jc>
3739       *    MyBean <jv>bean</jv> = <jv>myBeanFuture</jv>.get();
3740       * </p>
3741       *
3742       * @param executorService The executor service.
3743       * @param shutdownOnClose Call {@link ExecutorService#shutdown()} when {@link RestClient#close()} is called.
3744       * @return This object.
3745       */
3746      @FluentSetter
3747      public Builder executorService(ExecutorService executorService, boolean shutdownOnClose) {
3748         this.executorService = executorService;
3749         this.executorServiceShutdownOnClose = shutdownOnClose;
3750         return this;
3751      }
3752
3753      /**
3754       * <i><l>RestClient</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Keep HttpClient open.
3755       *
3756       * <p>
3757       * Don't close this client when the {@link RestClient#close()} method is called.
3758       *
3759       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3760       * <p class='bjava'>
3761       *    <jc>// Create a client with a customized client and don't close the client  service.</jc>
3762       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3763       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3764       *       .httpClient(<jv>myHttpClient</jv>)
3765       *       .keepHttpClientOpen()
3766       *       .build();
3767       *
3768       *    <jv>client</jv>.closeQuietly();  <jc>// Customized HttpClient won't be closed.</jc>
3769       * </p>
3770       *
3771       * @return This object.
3772       */
3773      @FluentSetter
3774      public Builder keepHttpClientOpen() {
3775         keepHttpClientOpen = true;
3776         return this;
3777      }
3778
3779      /**
3780       * Ignore errors.
3781       *
3782       * <p>
3783       * When enabled, HTTP error response codes (e.g. <l>&gt;=400</l>) will not cause a {@link RestCallException} to
3784       * be thrown.
3785       * <p>
3786       * Note that this is equivalent to <c>builder.errorCodes(x -&gt; <jk>false</jk>);</c>
3787       *
3788       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3789       * <p class='bjava'>
3790       *    <jc>// Create a client that doesn't throws a RestCallException when a 500 error occurs.</jc>
3791       *    RestClient
3792       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3793       *       .ignoreErrors()
3794       *       .build()
3795       *       .get(<js>"/error"</js>)  <jc>// Throws a 500 error</jc>
3796       *       .run()
3797       *       .assertStatus().is(500);
3798       * </p>
3799       *
3800       * @return This object.
3801       */
3802      @FluentSetter
3803      public Builder ignoreErrors() {
3804         ignoreErrors = true;
3805         return this;
3806      }
3807
3808      /**
3809       * <i><l>RestClient</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Call interceptors.
3810       *
3811       * <p>
3812       * Adds an interceptor that can be called to hook into specified events in the lifecycle of a single request.
3813       *
3814       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3815       * <p class='bjava'>
3816       *   <jc>// Customized interceptor (note you can also extend from BasicRestCallInterceptor as well.</jc>
3817       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyRestCallInterceptor <jk>implements</jk> RestCallInterceptor {
3818       *
3819       *       <ja>@Override</ja>
3820       *       <jk>public void</jk> onInit(RestRequest <jv>req</jv>) <jk>throws</jk> Exception {
3821       *       <jc>// Intercept immediately after RestRequest object is created and all headers/query/form-data has been
3822       *       // set on the request from the client.</jc>
3823       *    }
3824       *
3825       *    <ja>@Override</ja>
3826       *    <jk>public void</jk> onConnect(RestRequest <jv>req</jv>, RestResponse <jv>res</jv>) <jk>throws</jk> Exception {
3827       *       <jc>// Intercept immediately after an HTTP response has been received.</jc>
3828       *    }
3829       *
3830       *    <ja>@Override</ja>
3831       *    <jk>public void</jk> onClose(RestRequest <jv>req</jv>, RestResponse <jv>res</jv>) <jk>throws</jk> Exception {
3832       *          <jc>// Intercept when the response body is consumed.</jc>
3833       *       }
3834       *    }
3835       *
3836       *    <jc>// Create a client with a customized interceptor.</jc>
3837       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3838       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3839       *       .interceptors(MyRestCallInterceptor.<jk>class</jk>)
3840       *       .build();
3841       * </p>
3842       *
3843       * <ul class='notes'>
3844       *    <li class='note'>The {@link RestClient#onInit(RestRequest)}, {@link RestClient#onConnect(RestRequest,RestResponse)}, and
3845       * {@link RestClient#onClose(RestRequest,RestResponse)} methods can also be overridden to produce the same results.
3846       * </ul>
3847       *
3848       * @param values
3849       *    The values to add to this setting.
3850       *    <br>Can be implementations of any of the following:
3851       *    <ul>
3852       *       <li class='jic'>{@link RestCallInterceptor}
3853       *       <li class='jic'>{@link HttpRequestInterceptor}
3854       *       <li class='jic'>{@link HttpResponseInterceptor}
3855       *    </ul>
3856       * @return This object.
3857       * @throws Exception If one or more interceptors could not be created.
3858       */
3859      @FluentSetter
3860      public Builder interceptors(Class<?>...values) throws Exception {
3861         for (Class<?> c : values) {
3862            ClassInfo ci = ClassInfo.of(c);
3863            if (ci != null) {
3864               if (ci.isChildOfAny(RestCallInterceptor.class, HttpRequestInterceptor.class, HttpResponseInterceptor.class))
3865                  interceptors(ci.newInstance());
3866               else
3867                  throw new ConfigException("Invalid class of type ''{0}'' passed to interceptors().", ci.getName());
3868            }
3869         }
3870         return this;
3871      }
3872
3873      /**
3874       * Call interceptors.
3875       *
3876       * <p>
3877       * Adds an interceptor that gets called immediately after a connection is made.
3878       *
3879       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3880       * <p class='bjava'>
3881       *    <jc>// Create a client with a customized interceptor.</jc>
3882       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3883       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3884       *       .interceptors(
3885       *          <jk>new</jk> RestCallInterceptor() {
3886       *
3887       *             <ja>@Override</ja>
3888       *             <jk>public void</jk> onInit(RestRequest <jv>req</jv>) <jk>throws</jk> Exception {
3889       *             <jc>// Intercept immediately after RestRequest object is created and all headers/query/form-data has been
3890       *             // set on the request from the client.</jc>
3891       *          }
3892       *
3893       *          <ja>@Override</ja>
3894       *          <jk>public void</jk> onConnect(RestRequest <jv>req</jv>, RestResponse <jv>res</jv>) <jk>throws</jk> Exception {
3895       *             <jc>// Intercept immediately after an HTTP response has been received.</jc>
3896       *          }
3897       *
3898       *          <ja>@Override</ja>
3899       *          <jk>public void</jk> onClose(RestRequest <jv>req</jv>, RestResponse <jv>res</jv>) <jk>throws</jk> Exception {
3900       *                <jc>// Intercept when the response body is consumed.</jc>
3901       *             }
3902       *          }
3903       *       )
3904       *       .build();
3905       * </p>
3906       *
3907       * <ul class='notes'>
3908       *    <li class='note'>The {@link RestClient#onInit(RestRequest)}, {@link RestClient#onConnect(RestRequest,RestResponse)}, and
3909       * {@link RestClient#onClose(RestRequest,RestResponse)} methods can also be overridden to produce the same results.
3910       * </ul>
3911       *
3912       * @param value
3913       *    The values to add to this setting.
3914       *    <br>Can be implementations of any of the following:
3915       *    <ul>
3916       *       <li class='jic'>{@link RestCallInterceptor}
3917       *       <li class='jic'>{@link HttpRequestInterceptor}
3918       *       <li class='jic'>{@link HttpResponseInterceptor}
3919       *    </ul>
3920       * @return This object.
3921       */
3922      @FluentSetter
3923      public Builder interceptors(Object...value) {
3924         List<RestCallInterceptor> l = list();
3925         for (Object o : value) {
3926            ClassInfo ci = ClassInfo.of(o);
3927            if (ci != null) {
3928               if (! ci.isChildOfAny(HttpRequestInterceptor.class, HttpResponseInterceptor.class, RestCallInterceptor.class))
3929                  throw new ConfigException("Invalid object of type ''{0}'' passed to interceptors().", ci.getName());
3930               if (o instanceof HttpRequestInterceptor)
3931                  addInterceptorLast((HttpRequestInterceptor)o);
3932               if (o instanceof HttpResponseInterceptor)
3933                  addInterceptorLast((HttpResponseInterceptor)o);
3934               if (o instanceof RestCallInterceptor)
3935                  l.add((RestCallInterceptor)o);
3936            }
3937         }
3938         if (interceptors == null)
3939            interceptors = l;
3940         else
3941            interceptors.addAll(0, l);
3942         return this;
3943      }
3944
3945      /**
3946       * <i><l>RestClient</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Enable leak detection.
3947       *
3948       * <p>
3949       * Enable client and request/response leak detection.
3950       *
3951       * <p>
3952       * Causes messages to be logged to the console if clients or request/response objects are not properly closed
3953       * when the <c>finalize</c> methods are invoked.
3954       *
3955       * <p>
3956       * Automatically enabled with {@link org.apache.juneau.Context.Builder#debug()}.
3957       *
3958       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3959       * <p class='bjava'>
3960       *    <jc>// Create a client that logs a message if </jc>
3961       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3962       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3963       *       .detectLeaks()
3964       *       .logToConsole()  <jc>// Also log the error message to System.err</jc>
3965       *       .build();
3966       *
3967       *    <jv>client</jv>.closeQuietly();  <jc>// Customized HttpClient won't be closed.</jc>
3968       * </p>
3969       *
3970       * @return This object.
3971       */
3972      @FluentSetter
3973      public Builder detectLeaks() {
3974         detectLeaks = true;
3975         return this;
3976      }

3978      /**
3979       * <i><l>RestClient</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Marshaller
3980       *
3981       * <p>
3982       * Shortcut for specifying the serializers and parsers
3983       * using the serializer and parser defined in a marshaller.
3984       *
3985       * <ul class='notes'>
3986       *    <li class='note'>When using this method that takes in a pre-instantiated serializers and parsers, the serializer property setters (e.g. {@link #sortCollections()}),
3987       *    parser property setters (e.g. {@link #strict()}), or bean context property setters (e.g. {@link #swaps(Class...)}) defined on this builder class have no effect.
3988       * </ul>
3989       *
3990       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
3991       * <p class='bjava'>
3992       *    <jc>// Create a client that uses Simplified-JSON transport using an existing marshaller.</jc>
3993       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
3994       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
3995       *       .marshaller(SimpleJson.<jsf>DEFAULT_READABLE</jsf>)
3996       *       .build();
3997       * </p>
3998       *
3999       * @param value The values to add to this setting.
4000       * @return This object.
4001       */
4002      @FluentSetter
4003      public Builder marshaller(Marshaller value) {
4004         if (value != null)
4005            serializer(value.getSerializer()).parser(value.getParser());
4006         return this;
4007      }

4009      /**
4010       * <i><l>RestClient</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Marshalls
4011       *
4012       * <p>
4013       * Shortcut for specifying the serializers and parsers
4014       * using the serializer and parser defined in a marshaller.
4015       *
4016       * <ul class='notes'>
4017       *    <li class='note'>When using this method that takes in a pre-instantiated serializers and parsers, the serializer property setters (e.g. {@link #sortCollections()}),
4018       *    parser property setters (e.g. {@link #strict()}), or bean context property setters (e.g. {@link #swaps(Class...)}) defined on this builder class have no effect.
4019       * </ul>
4020       *
4021       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4022       * <p class='bjava'>
4023       *    <jc>// Create a client that uses JSON and XML transport using existing marshalls.</jc>
4024       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4025       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4026       *       .marshaller(Json.<jsf>DEFAULT_READABLE</jsf>, Xml.<jsf>DEFAULT_READABLE</jsf>)
4027       *       .build();
4028       * </p>
4029       *
4030       * @param value The values to add to this setting.
4031       * @return This object.
4032       */
4033      @FluentSetter
4034      public Builder marshallers(Marshaller...value) {
4035         for (Marshaller m : value)
4036            if (m != null)
4037               serializer(m.getSerializer()).parser(m.getParser());
4038         return this;
4039      }

4041      /**
4042       * <i><l>RestClient</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Root URI.
4043       *
4044       * <p>
4045       * When set, relative URI strings passed in through the various rest call methods (e.g. {@link RestClient#get(Object)}
4046       * will be prefixed with the specified root.
4047       * <br>This root URI is ignored on those methods if you pass in a {@link URL}, {@link URI}, or an absolute URI string.
4048       *
4049       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4050       * <p class='bjava'>
4051       *    <jc>// Create a client that uses UON format by default for HTTP parts.</jc>
4052       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4053       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4054       *       .rootUri(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>)
4055       *       .build();
4056       *
4057       *    Bar <jv>bar</jv> = <jv>client</jv>
4058       *       .get(<js>"/bar"</js>)  <jc>// Relative to http://localhost:10000/foo</jc>
4059       *       .run()
4060       *       .getContent().as(Bar.<jk>class</jk>);
4061       * </p>
4062       *
4063       * @param value
4064       *    The root URI to prefix to relative URI strings.
4065       *    <br>Trailing slashes are trimmed.
4066       *    <br>Usually a <c>String</c> but you can also pass in <c>URI</c> and <c>URL</c> objects as well.
4067       * @return This object.
4068       */
4069      @FluentSetter
4070      public Builder rootUri(Object value) {
4071         String s = stringify(value);
4072         if (! isEmpty(s))
4073            s = s.replaceAll("\\/$", "");
4074         if (isEmpty(s))
4075            rootUri = null;
4076         else if (s.indexOf("://") == -1)
4077            throw runtimeException("Invalid rootUri value: ''{0}''.  Must be a valid absolute URL.", value);
4078         else
4079            rootUri = s;
4080         return this;
4081      }
4082
4083      /**
4084       * Returns the root URI defined for this client.
4085       *
4086       * <p>
4087       * Returns <jk>null</jk> in leu of an empty string.
4088       * Trailing slashes are trimmed.
4089       *
4090       * @return The root URI defined for this client.
4091       */
4092      public String getRootUri() {
4093         return rootUri;
4094      }

4214      /**
4215       * <i><l>BeanTraverse</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Automatically detect POJO recursions.
4216       *
4217       * <p>
4218       * When enabled, specifies that recursions should be checked for during traversal.
4219       *
4220       * <p>
4221       * Recursions can occur when traversing models that aren't true trees but rather contain loops.
4222       * <br>In general, unchecked recursions cause stack-overflow-errors.
4223       * <br>These show up as {@link BeanRecursionException BeanRecursionException} with the message <js>"Depth too deep.  Stack overflow occurred."</js>.
4224       *
4225       * <ul class='notes'>
4226       *    <li class='note'>
4227       *       Checking for recursion can cause a small performance penalty.
4228       * </ul>
4229       *
4230       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4231       * <p class='bjava'>
4232       *    <jc>// Create a JSON client that automatically checks for recursions.</jc>
4233       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4234       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4235       *       .json()
4236       *       .detectRecursions()
4237       *       .build();
4238       *
4239       *    <jc>// Create a POJO model with a recursive loop.</jc>
4240       *    <jk>public class</jk> A {
4241       *       <jk>public</jk> Object <jf>f</jf>;
4242       *    }
4243       *    A <jv>a</jv> = <jk>new</jk> A();
4244       *    <jv>a</jv>.<jf>f</jf> = <jv>a</jv>;
4245       *
4246       * <jk>try</jk> {
4247       *       <jc>// Throws a RestCallException with an inner SerializeException and not a StackOverflowError</jc>
4248       *       <jv>client</jv>
4249       *          .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jv>a</jv>)
4250       *          .run();
4251       * } <jk>catch</jk> (RestCallException <jv>e</jv>} {
4252       *    <jc>// Handle exception.</jc>
4253       * }
4254       * </p>
4255       *
4256       * <ul class='seealso'>
4257       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.BeanTraverseContext.Builder#detectRecursions()}
4258       * </ul>
4259       *
4260       * @return This object.
4261       */
4262      @FluentSetter
4263      public Builder detectRecursions() {
4264         serializers().forEach(x -> x.detectRecursions());
4265         return this;
4266      }
4267
4268      /**
4269       * <i><l>BeanTraverse</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Ignore recursion errors.
4270       *
4271       * <p>
4272       * When enabled, when we encounter the same object when traversing a tree, we set the value to <jk>null</jk>.
4273       *
4274       * <p>
4275       * For example, if a model contains the links A-&gt;B-&gt;C-&gt;A, then the JSON generated will look like
4276       *    the following when <jsf>BEANTRAVERSE_ignoreRecursions</jsf> is <jk>true</jk>...
4277       *
4278       * <p class='bjson'>
4279       *    {A:{B:{C:<jk>null</jk>}}}
4280       * </p>
4281       *
4282       * <ul class='notes'>
4283       *    <li class='note'>
4284       *       Checking for recursion can cause a small performance penalty.
4285       * </ul>
4286       *
4287       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4288       * <p class='bjava'>
4289       *    <jc>// Create a JSON client that ignores recursions.</jc>
4290       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4291       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4292       *       .json()
4293       *       .ignoreRecursions()
4294       *       .build();
4295       *
4296       *    <jc>// Create a POJO model with a recursive loop.</jc>
4297       *    <jk>public class</jk> A {
4298       *       <jk>public</jk> Object <jf>f</jf>;
4299       *    }
4300       *    A <jv>a</jv> = <jk>new</jk> A();
4301       *    <jv>a</jv>.<jf>f</jf> = <jv>a</jv>;
4302       *
4303       *    <jc>// Produces request body "{f:null}"</jc>
4304       *    <jv>client</jv>
4305       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jv>a</jv>)
4306       *       .run();
4307       * </p>
4308       *
4309       * <ul class='seealso'>
4310       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.BeanTraverseContext.Builder#ignoreRecursions()}
4311       * </ul>
4312       *
4313       * @return This object.
4314       */
4315      @FluentSetter
4316      public Builder ignoreRecursions() {
4317         serializers().forEach(x -> x.ignoreRecursions());
4318         return this;
4319      }
4320
4321      /**
4322       * <i><l>BeanTraverse</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Initial depth.
4323       *
4324       * <p>
4325       * The initial indentation level at the root.
4326       *
4327       * <p>
4328       * Useful when constructing document fragments that need to be indented at a certain level when whitespace is enabled.
4329       *
4330       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4331       * <p class='bjava'>
4332       *    <jc>// Create a REST client with JSON serializer with whitespace enabled and an initial depth of 2.</jc>
4333       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4334       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4335       *       .json()
4336       *       .ws()
4337       *       .initialDepth(2)
4338       *       .build();
4339       *
4340       *    <jc>// Our bean to serialize.</jc>
4341       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyBean {
4342       *       <jk>public</jk> String <jf>foo</jf> = <jk>null</jk>;
4343       *    }
4344       *
4345       *    <jc>// Produces request body "\t\t{\n\t\t\t'foo':'bar'\n\t\t}\n"</jc>
4346       *    <jv>client</jv>
4347       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jk>new</jk> MyBean())
4348       *       .run();
4349       * </p>
4350       *
4351       * <ul class='seealso'>
4352       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.BeanTraverseContext.Builder#initialDepth(int)}
4353       * </ul>
4354       *
4355       * @param value
4356       *    The new value for this property.
4357       *    <br>The default is <c>0</c>.
4358       * @return This object.
4359       */
4360      @FluentSetter
4361      public Builder initialDepth(int value) {
4362         serializers().forEach(x -> x.initialDepth(value));
4363         return this;
4364      }

4366      /**
4367       * <i><l>BeanTraverse</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Max serialization depth.
4368       *
4369       * <p>
4370       * When enabled, abort traversal if specified depth is reached in the POJO tree.
4371       *
4372       * <p>
4373       * If this depth is exceeded, an exception is thrown.
4374       *
4375       * <p>
4376       * This prevents stack overflows from occurring when trying to traverse models with recursive references.
4377       *
4378       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4379       * <p class='bjava'>
4380       *    <jc>// Create a REST client with JSON serializer that throws an exception if the depth reaches greater than 20.</jc>
4381       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4382       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4383       *       .json()
4384       *       .maxDepth(20)
4385       *       .build();
4386       * </p>
4387       *
4388       * <ul class='seealso'>
4389       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.BeanTraverseContext.Builder#maxDepth(int)}
4390       * </ul>
4391       *
4392       * @param value
4393       *    The new value for this property.
4394       *    <br>The default is <c>100</c>.
4395       * @return This object.
4396       */
4397      @FluentSetter
4398      public Builder maxDepth(int value) {
4399         serializers().forEach(x -> x.maxDepth(value));
4400         return this;
4401      }

4407      /**
4408       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Add <js>"_type"</js> properties when needed.
4409       *
4410       * <p>
4411       * When enabled, <js>"_type"</js> properties will be added to beans if their type cannot be inferred
4412       * through reflection.
4413       *
4414       * <p>
4415       * This is used to recreate the correct objects during parsing if the object types cannot be inferred.
4416       * <br>For example, when serializing a <c>Map&lt;String,Object&gt;</c> field where the bean class cannot be determined from
4417       * the type of the values.
4418       *
4419       * <p>
4420       * Note the differences between the following settings:
4421       * <ul class='javatree'>
4422       *    <li class='jf'>{@link #addRootType()} - Affects whether <js>'_type'</js> is added to root node.
4423       *    <li class='jf'>{@link #addBeanTypes()} - Affects whether <js>'_type'</js> is added to any nodes.
4424       * </ul>
4425       *
4426       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4427       * <p class='bjava'>
4428       *    <jc>// Create a JSON client that adds _type to nodes in the request body.</jc>
4429       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4430       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4431       *       .json()
4432       *       .addBeanTypes()
4433       *       .build();
4434       *
4435       *    <jc>// Our map of beans to serialize.</jc>
4436       *    <ja>@Bean</ja>(typeName=<js>"mybean"</js>)
4437       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyBean {
4438       *       <jk>public</jk> String <jf>foo</jf> = <js>"bar"</js>;
4439       *    }
4440       *
4441       *    AMap <jv>map</jv> = AMap.of(<js>"foo"</js>, <jk>new</jk> MyBean());
4442       *
4443       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  {"foo":{"_type":"mybean","foo":"bar"}}</jc>
4444       *    <jv>client</jv>
4445       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jv>map</jv>)
4446       *       .run();
4447       * </p>
4448       *
4449       * <ul class='seealso'>
4450       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#addBeanTypes()}
4451       * </ul>
4452       *
4453       * @return This object.
4454       */
4455      @FluentSetter
4456      public Builder addBeanTypes() {
4457         serializers().forEach(x -> x.addBeanTypes());
4458         return this;
4459      }
4460
4461      /**
4462       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Add type attribute to root nodes.
4463       *
4464       * <p>
4465       * When enabled, <js>"_type"</js> properties will be added to top-level beans.
4466       *
4467       * <p>
4468       * When disabled, it is assumed that the parser knows the exact Java POJO type being parsed, and therefore top-level
4469       * type information that might normally be included to determine the data type will not be serialized.
4470       *
4471       * <p>
4472       * For example, when serializing a top-level POJO with a {@link Bean#typeName() @Bean(typeName)} value, a
4473       * <js>'_type'</js> attribute will only be added when this setting is enabled.
4474       *
4475       * <p>
4476       * Note the differences between the following settings:
4477       * <ul class='javatree'>
4478       *    <li class='jf'>{@link #addRootType()} - Affects whether <js>'_type'</js> is added to root node.
4479       *    <li class='jf'>{@link #addBeanTypes()} - Affects whether <js>'_type'</js> is added to any nodes.
4480       * </ul>
4481       *
4482       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4483       * <p class='bjava'>
4484       *    <jc>// Create a JSON client that adds _type to root node.</jc>
4485       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4486       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4487       *       .json()
4488       *       .addRootType()
4489       *       .build();
4490       *
4491       *    <jc>// Our bean to serialize.</jc>
4492       *    <ja>@Bean</ja>(typeName=<js>"mybean"</js>)
4493       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyBean {
4494       *       <jk>public</jk> String <jf>foo</jf> = <js>"bar"</js>;
4495       *    }
4496       *
4497       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  {"_type":"mybean","foo":"bar"}</jc>
4498       *    <jv>client</jv>
4499       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jk>new</jk> MyBean())
4500       *       .run();
4501       * </p>
4502       *
4503       * <ul class='seealso'>
4504       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#addRootType()}
4505       * </ul>
4506       *
4507       * @return This object.
4508       */
4509      @FluentSetter
4510      public Builder addRootType() {
4511         serializers().forEach(x -> x.addRootType());
4512         return this;
4513      }
4514
4515      /**
4516       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Don't trim null bean property values.
4517       *
4518       * <p>
4519       * When enabled, null bean values will be serialized to the output.
4520       *
4521       * <ul class='notes'>
4522       *    <li class='note'>Not enabling this setting will cause <c>Map</c>s with <jk>null</jk> values to be lost during parsing.
4523       * </ul>
4524       *
4525       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4526       * <p class='bjava'>
4527       *    <jc>// Create a REST client with JSON serializer that serializes null properties.</jc>
4528       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4529       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4530       *       .json()
4531       *       .keepNullProperties()
4532       *       .build();
4533       *
4534       *    <jc>// Our bean to serialize.</jc>
4535       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyBean {
4536       *       <jk>public</jk> String <jf>foo</jf> = <jk>null</jk>;
4537       *    }
4538       *
4539       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  {foo:null}</jc>
4540       *    <jv>client</jv>
4541       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jk>new</jk> MyBean())
4542       *       .run();
4543       * </p>
4544       *
4545       * <ul class='seealso'>
4546       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#keepNullProperties()}
4547       * </ul>
4548       *
4549       * @return This object.
4550       */
4551      @FluentSetter
4552      public Builder keepNullProperties() {
4553         serializers().forEach(x -> x.keepNullProperties());
4554         return this;
4555      }

4557      /**
4558       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Sort arrays and collections alphabetically.
4559       *
4560       * <p>
4561       * When enabled, copies and sorts the contents of arrays and collections before serializing them.
4562       *
4563       * <p>
4564       * Note that this introduces a performance penalty since it requires copying the existing collection.
4565       *
4566       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4567       * <p class='bjava'>
4568       *    <jc>// Create a REST client with JSON serializer that sorts arrays and collections before serialization.</jc>
4569       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4570       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4571       *       .json()
4572       *       .sortCollections()
4573       *       .build();
4574       *
4575       *    <jc>// An unsorted array</jc>
4576       *    String[] <jv>array</jv> = {<js>"foo"</js>,<js>"bar"</js>,<js>"baz"</js>}
4577       *
4578       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  ["bar","baz","foo"]</jc>
4579       *    <jv>client</jv>
4580       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jv>array</jv>)
4581       *       .run();
4582       * </p>
4583       *
4584       * <ul class='seealso'>
4585       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#sortCollections()}
4586       * </ul>
4587       *
4588       * @return This object.
4589       */
4590      @FluentSetter
4591      public Builder sortCollections() {
4592         serializers().forEach(x -> x.sortCollections());
4593         return this;
4594      }

4596      /**
4597       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Sort maps alphabetically.
4598       *
4599       * <p>
4600       * When enabled, copies and sorts the contents of maps by their keys before serializing them.
4601       *
4602       * <p>
4603       * Note that this introduces a performance penalty.
4604       *
4605       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4606       * <p class='bjava'>
4607       *    <jc>// Create a REST client with JSON serializer that sorts maps before serialization.</jc>
4608       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4609       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4610       *       .json()
4611       *       .sortMaps()
4612       *       .build();
4613       *
4614       *    <jc>// An unsorted map.</jc>
4615       *    AMap <jv>map</jv> = AMap.<jsm>of</jsm>(<js>"foo"</js>,1,<js>"bar"</js>,2,<js>"baz"</js>,3);
4616       *
4617       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  {"bar":2,"baz":3,"foo":1}</jc>
4618       *    <jv>client</jv>
4619       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jv>map</jv>)
4620       *       .run();
4621       * </p>
4622       *
4623       * <ul class='seealso'>
4624       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#sortMaps()}
4625       * </ul>
4626       *
4627       * @return This object.
4628       */
4629      @FluentSetter
4630      public Builder sortMaps() {
4631         serializers().forEach(x -> x.sortMaps());
4632         return this;
4633      }

4635      /**
4636       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Trim empty lists and arrays.
4637       *
4638       * <p>
4639       * When enabled, empty lists and arrays will not be serialized.
4640       *
4641       * <p>
4642       * Note that enabling this setting has the following effects on parsing:
4643       * <ul class='spaced-list'>
4644       *    <li>
4645       *       Map entries with empty list values will be lost.
4646       *    <li>
4647       *       Bean properties with empty list values will not be set.
4648       * </ul>
4649       *
4650       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4651       * <p class='bjava'>
4652       *    <jc>// Create a serializer that skips empty arrays and collections.</jc>
4653       *    WriterSerializer <jv>serializer</jv> = JsonSerializer
4654       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4655       *       .trimEmptyCollections()
4656       *       .build();
4657       *
4658       *    <jc>// A bean with a field with an empty array.</jc>
4659       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyBean {
4660       *       <jk>public</jk> String[] <jf>foo</jf> = {};
4661       *    }
4662       *
4663       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  {}</jc>
4664       *    <jv>client</jv>
4665       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jk>new</jk> MyBean())
4666       *       .run();
4667       * </p>
4668       *
4669       * <ul class='seealso'>
4670       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#trimEmptyCollections()}
4671       * </ul>
4672       *
4673       * @return This object.
4674       */
4675      @FluentSetter
4676      public Builder trimEmptyCollections() {
4677         serializers().forEach(x -> x.trimEmptyCollections());
4678         return this;
4679      }

4762      /**
4763       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  URI context bean.
4764       *
4765       * <p>
4766       * Bean used for resolution of URIs to absolute or root-relative form.
4767       *
4768       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4769       * <p class='bjava'>
4770       *    <jc>// Our URI contextual information.</jc>
4771       *    String <jv>authority</jv> = <js>"http://localhost:10000"</js>;
4772       *    String <jv>contextRoot</jv> = <js>"/myContext"</js>;
4773       *    String <jv>servletPath</jv> = <js>"/myServlet"</js>;
4774       *    String <jv>pathInfo</jv> = <js>"/foo"</js>;
4775       *
4776       *    <jc>// Create a UriContext object.</jc>
4777       *    UriContext <jv>uriContext</jv> = <jk>new</jk> UriContext(<jv>authority</jv>, <jv>contextRoot</jv>, <jv>servletPath</jv>, <jv>pathInfo</jv>);
4778       *
4779       *    <jc>// Create a REST client with JSON serializer and associate our context.</jc>
4780       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4781       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4782       *       .json()
4783       *       .uriContext(<jv>uriContext</jv>)
4784       *       .uriRelativity(<jsf>RESOURCE</jsf>)  <jc>// Assume relative paths are relative to servlet.</jc>
4785       *       .uriResolution(<jsf>ABSOLUTE</jsf>)  <jc>// Serialize URIs as absolute paths.</jc>
4786       *       .build();
4787       *
4788       *    <jc>// A relative URI</jc>
4789       *    URI <jv>uri</jv> = <jk>new</jk> URI(<js>"bar"</js>);
4790       *
4791       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  "http://localhost:10000/myContext/myServlet/foo/bar"</jc>
4792       *    <jv>client</jv>
4793       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jv>uri</jv>)
4794       *       .run();
4795       * </p>
4796       *
4797       * <ul class='seealso'>
4798       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#uriContext(UriContext)}
4799       *    <li class='link'>{@doc jm.MarshallingUris}
4800       * </ul>
4801       *
4802       * @param value The new value for this property.
4803       * @return This object.
4804       */
4805      @FluentSetter
4806      public Builder uriContext(UriContext value) {
4807         serializers().forEach(x -> x.uriContext(value));
4808         return this;
4809      }

4811      /**
4812       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  URI relativity.
4813       *
4814       * <p>
4815       * Defines what relative URIs are relative to when serializing any of the following:
4816       * <ul>
4817       *    <li>{@link java.net.URI}
4818       *    <li>{@link java.net.URL}
4819       *    <li>Properties and classes annotated with {@link Uri @Uri}
4820       * </ul>
4821       *
4822       * <p>
4823       * See {@link #uriContext(UriContext)} for examples.
4824       *
4825       * <ul class='values javatree'>
4826       *    <li class='jf'>{@link org.apache.juneau.UriRelativity#RESOURCE}
4827       *       - Relative URIs should be considered relative to the servlet URI.
4828       *    <li class='jf'>{@link org.apache.juneau.UriRelativity#PATH_INFO}
4829       *       - Relative URIs should be considered relative to the request URI.
4830       * </ul>
4831       *
4832       * <ul class='seealso'>
4833       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#uriRelativity(UriRelativity)}
4834       *    <li class='link'>{@doc jm.MarshallingUris}
4835       * </ul>
4836       *
4837       * @param value
4838       *    The new value for this property.
4839       *    <br>The default is {@link UriRelativity#RESOURCE}
4840       * @return This object.
4841       */
4842      @FluentSetter
4843      public Builder uriRelativity(UriRelativity value) {
4844         serializers().forEach(x -> x.uriRelativity(value));
4845         return this;
4846      }

4849       * <i><l>Serializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  URI resolution.
4850       *
4851       * <p>
4852       * Defines the resolution level for URIs when serializing any of the following:
4853       * <ul>
4854       *    <li>{@link java.net.URI}
4855       *    <li>{@link java.net.URL}
4856       *    <li>Properties and classes annotated with {@link Uri @Uri}
4857       * </ul>
4858       *
4859       * <p>
4860       * See {@link #uriContext(UriContext)} for examples.
4861       *
4862       * <ul class='values'>

4864       *       - Resolve to an absolute URI (e.g. <js>"http://host:port/context-root/servlet-path/path-info"</js>).
4865       *    <li class='jf'>{@link UriResolution#ROOT_RELATIVE}
4866       *       - Resolve to a root-relative URI (e.g. <js>"/context-root/servlet-path/path-info"</js>).
4867       *    <li class='jf'>{@link UriResolution#NONE}
4868       *       - Don't do any URI resolution.
4869       * </ul>
4870       *
4871       * <ul class='seealso'>
4872       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.Serializer.Builder#uriResolution(UriResolution)}
4873       *    <li class='link'>{@doc jm.MarshallingUris}
4874       * </ul>
4875       *
4876       * @param value
4877       *    The new value for this property.
4878       *    <br>The default is {@link UriResolution#NONE}
4879       * @return This object.
4880       */
4881      @FluentSetter
4882      public Builder uriResolution(UriResolution value) {
4883         serializers().forEach(x -> x.uriResolution(value));
4884         return this;
4885      }

4927      /**
4928       * <i><l>WriterSerializer</l> configuration property:&emsp;</i>  Quote character.
4929       *
4930       * <p>
4931       * Specifies the character to use for quoting attributes and values.
4932       *
4933       * <ul class='notes'>
4934       *    <li class='note'>This setting does not apply to the RDF serializers.
4935       * </ul>
4936       *
4937       * <h5 class='section'>Example:</h5>
4938       * <p class='bjava'>
4939       *    <jc>// Create a REST client with JSON serializer that uses single quotes.</jc>
4940       *    RestClient <jv>client</jv> = RestClient
4941       *       .<jsm>create</jsm>()
4942       *       .json()
4943       *       .quoteChar(<js>'\''</js>)
4944       *       .build();
4945       *
4946       *    <jc>// A bean with a single property</jc>
4947       *    <jk>public class</jk> MyBean {
4948       *       <jk>public</jk> String <jf>foo</jf> = <js>"bar"</js>;
4949       *    }
4950       *
4951       *    <jc>// Request body will contain:  {'foo':'bar'}</jc>
4952       *    <jv>client</jv>
4953       *       .post(<js>"http://localhost:10000/foo"</js>, <jk>new</jk> MyBean())
4954       *       .run();
4955       * </p>
4956       *
4957       * <ul class='seealso'>
4958       *    <li class='jm'>{@link org.apache.juneau.serializer.WriterSerializer.Builder#quoteChar(char)}
4959       * </ul>
4960       *
4961       * @param value
4962       *    The new value for this property.
4963       *    <br>The default is <js>'"'</js>.
4964       * @return This object.
4965       */
4966      @FluentSetter
4967      public Builder quoteChar(char value) {
4968         serializers().forEachWS(x -> x.quoteChar(value));
4969         return this;
4970      }

4999       *       .run();
